# 16 ŌĆö Dispatcher Backlog

Working backlog for items extracted from `input/input_raw.md`. Each row
points to the originating line range so context is recoverable.

**Convention:** items are dispatched in rounds; each round runs as one
or more parallel sub-agents on the
`claude/implement-input-raw-changes-2WiOF` branch (or worktree of it).
Status legend:

- `queued` ŌĆö vetted, waiting for dispatch slot
- `in-progress` ŌĆö agent is working (note round + agent ID/branch)
- `done` ŌĆö landed in this branch (commit hash)
- `blocked` ŌĆö needs user input (note reason)
- `parked` ŌĆö out of scope for this branch (e.g. dataship work, infra)

## Scope filter

`input_raw.md` mixes work for at least three projects:

1. `dlr-shepard/shepard` (this repo, Java/Quarkus backend + Nuxt 3 / Vue 3 /
   Vuetify 3 frontend + client libs) ŌĆö **in scope**. (Earlier rounds said
   "Angular"; corrected by the `aidocs/33` agent which verified against
   `frontend/package.json:24,45-46`.)
2. `dlr-shepard/shepard-dataship` (separate Python client; M1ŌĆōM9 milestones
   on lines 975ŌĆō1214 reference `src/ui/*.py`, `src/worker.py`, etc.) ŌĆö
   **out of scope here**, parked.
3. Program-level work (HMC, federation, project website, AAS) ŌĆö **parked**,
   not implementable from this repo.

## Backlog (this repo only)

| PM1b3 | True runtime CDI integration ŌĆö a vendor drops `shepard-plugin-foo-x.y.z.jar` into `/deployments/plugins/` at runtime and its REST endpoints + admin CLI subcommand come up **without** declaring the plugin in the backend's `with-plugins` Maven profile. Option B (per the `aidocs/69` analysis): extend `PluginContext` with `registerHttpRoute(pathPattern, handler)` so plugins ship Vert.x handlers instead of `@Path` resources (side-steps Quarkus's build-time CDI scanning); wire `PluginRegistry` to a singleton `PluginRouter` that manages the live Vert.x route table. PM1b2's `DEGRADED` state becomes the auto-detection signal: a JAR-walk plugin without a matching `quarkus.index-dependency.*` config key lands DEGRADED with `plugin.runtime.no-cdi-scan` and the failureMessage points at the runbook. Ship a vendor-style example plugin (`plugins/example-video/`) that's NOT in the `with-plugins` profile, demonstrating the drop-in path end-to-end. | `aidocs/69 ┬¦4`, ADR-0023 forward-work | M-L | queued | Quarkus's build-time CDI scanner doesn't expose a runtime bean-addition API (verified against Quarkus 3.27.x source); the structurally correct fix is to give plugins a non-CDI HTTP-handler shape. See `aidocs/69` for the full reasoning + the Option A (per-plugin Quarkus extension) vs Option B (Vert.x router) trade-off. |

End-user UX byte-identical ŌĆö `shepard-admin unhide ŌĆ”` works exactly as before; same verbs, same flags, same JSON shapes, same exit codes; the 12 UnhideCommandsTest cases run unmodified in their new location (only their package + the parent-wiring assertion were updated to call `ShepardAdmin.commandLine()` so the SPI discovery runs). 5 new `AdminCliCommandProviderTest` cases on the JAR-walk path (synthetic plugin JAR built inline via the Java compiler API + a fail-fast smoke through the bootstrap), 4 new `ShepardAdminBootstrapTest` cases on the wiring (core subcommands intact, idempotent, --help, --version). Pre-existing CLI bug fix continuity: the duplicate `delete(String)` overload PM1b already removed stays removed. **Backend untouched**: PM1d is a `cli/`-side + `plugins/`-side refactor only. **Test obligation deferred**: an integration regression that drives `java -jar shepard-admin.jar unhide status` end-to-end against a live Quarkus instance is queued alongside the broader PM1a/PM1b testcontainer story. |

### Newly surfaced (second-pass analysis of `input_raw.md` lines 1840ŌĆō8409)

These come from a re-read of regions the first scan missed. `R7` deduplicates with existing `L1`. `R2` (RO-Crate) is **already implemented** in this repo (`ExportConstants.ROCRATE_METADATA`); only the per-payload selection enhancement remains. Most others are blocked on user/maintainer decisions.

| ID | Item | input_raw refs | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| R1 | Databus + MOSS federation layer (`shepard-plugin-databus`) | 8380 | M | **design done** | `aidocs/77`. Full design: `:DatabusConfig` admin entity, admin REST + CLI parity, researcher-facing `POST /v2/collections/{appId}/publish/databus`, PROV-O Turtle generation, `shepard` MOSS module definition (SHACL + indexer). MB1aŌĆōMB1g phasing. Gated on PROV1a (`:Activity` capture, `aidocs/55`) and the MOSS module YAML landing in the DLR-internal Databus instance. |
| R2 | Per-payload selective RO-Crate export (refinement of existing export) | 8381 | SŌĆōM | **Phase 1 done** | Round 6, commit `be0eb26` (cherry-picked). Existing exporter lives in `backend/src/main/java/de/dlr/shepard/context/export/` (`ExportService` is the walker entry point, `ExportBuilder` wraps `edu.kit.datamanager.ro_crate.RoCrate.RoCrateBuilder`). Phase 1 adds an optional `ExportSelection` body on a **new** sibling `POST /collections/{collectionId}/export` (the existing GET is preserved unchanged for byte-identical legacy behaviour). Selection has two sections: `payloads` (`include` allow-list of kinds + `excludeIds` deny-list) and `metadata` booleans (permissions / annotations / labJournal / versions / subscriptions). The selection actually applied is recorded as a JSON block on the root data entity in `ro-crate-metadata.json` so consumers can tell what was excluded. 18 tests pass (5 new selection-service + 2 new manifest-injection + 11 pre-existing). **Important:** the exporter today does **not** yet emit `permissions / versions / subscriptions / annotations` documents ŌĆö the booleans are wired and recorded but bundling those metadata kinds is deferred to **R2d**. |
| R2b | File- and column-level selection on payloads (per-FileReference oid include list; per-TimeseriesReference column / time-window picks) | ŌĆö | M | done | Round 6, commit `60a3ea1`. Adds `payloads.perPayload: Map<entityId, PerPayloadSelection>` and `payloads.strictPerPayload: boolean`. `PerPayloadSelection` has optional `fileOids`, `columns`, `timeRange{start,end}` ŌĆö kind-applicability is silent (wrong-kind entries ignored). Existing per-OID file-fetch service reused; existing `fieldFilterSet` parameter on `TimeseriesReferenceService.exportReferencedTimeseriesByShepardId` covers per-column projection; a new 14-arg overload accepts `startNanosOverride` / `endNanosOverride` for time-window without mutating the reference. Stale OIDs / unknown columns silently skipped + recorded in a new `selection.warnings[]` array on the manifest's root selection block; `strictPerPayload=true` flips that to 400. 11 new tests pass (43/43 export-package). P17b lint stays green. |
| R2c | Per-payload metadata-field redaction (e.g. include the annotation but redact its label) | ŌĆö | M | done | Round 6, commit `f993e8b`. Adds `metadata.redactFields: Set<RedactableField>` to `ExportSelection`. **Closed enum** of 6 fields, each verified against the actual IO type before shipping (one stop-and-report adjustment): `PERMISSION_USERNAME` (replaces `owner` + `reader[]` + `writer[]` + `manager[]`), `PERMISSION_GROUP_IDS` (empties `readerGroupIds` / `writerGroupIds` ŌĆö renamed from proposed `ŌĆ”_GROUP_NAME` because `PermissionsIO` carries group ids only), `ANNOTATION_LABEL` (replaces `propertyName` ŌĆö proposed `label` doesn't exist; IRI left intact as stable id), `ANNOTATION_VALUE` (replaces `valueName` ŌĆö proposed `value` doesn't exist), `VERSION_AUTHOR` (replaces `createdBy` ŌĆö no `author` field), `LAB_JOURNAL_CONTENT` (replaces `journalContent`). Mutation is direct setter on the Lombok `@Data` IO types before serialisation. Manifest selection block records the **set** but not the replacement values (no leak vector). 11 new tests pass; 54/54 export-package total. |
| R2d | Emit permissions / versions / subscriptions / semantic-annotations documents from the exporter (the metadata booleans from R2 Phase 1 are wired but the exporter currently doesn't bundle these doc kinds) | ŌĆö | M | **mostly done** | Round 6, commit `d5fa03c`. **3 of 4 kinds wired:** `permissions` (via `PermissionsService.getPermissionsOfEntityOptional`), `versions` (via `VersionService.getAllVersions`; collection-only ŌĆö only Collections are versioned), `annotations` (via `BasicEntity.getAnnotations()`). Defaults remain `false` so today's behaviour is unchanged. 14 new tests pass on merged branch (10 service-level in `ExportMetadataBundleTest`, 4 builder-level in `ExportBuilderSelectionTest`). **`subscriptions` deferred** ŌĆö see **R2d2** below. |
| R2d2 | Emit per-entity subscriptions in the RO-Crate export ŌĆö needs a URL-pattern ŌåÆ entity-URL matcher because subscriptions in shepard are URL-pattern-based, not per-entity-attached | ŌĆö | M | done | Round 6, commit `967fbf5`. New `SubscriptionMatcher` extracted from `SubscriptionFilter` (pure refactor; `SubscriptionFilterTest` 7/7 pass); new `EntityUrlSynthesiser` produces canonical paths for Collection / DataObject / BasicReference / LabJournalEntry using the same `Constants.*` tokens the JAX-RS resources use. Walker hook calls `subscriptionService.getMatchingSubscriptionsForUrl(url, method)` and writes `<id>-subscriptions.json` per entity. **Documented trade-off:** subscription patterns are full-URL regexes (scheme + host); export only knows the path, so authors of host-anchored patterns may need a `.*` prefix to also match exports. 7 new tests pass; 43+ on merged branch. |

## Open user decisions (blocking some items)

1. **Leaked JWTs** at `aidocs/input/input_raw.md:222` and `:360` (issuers
   `bt-au-cube2.intra.dlr.de`, `bt-au-cube3.intra.dlr.de`, sub `kreb_fl`).
   Already on `origin`. Need: rotate tokens, decide whether to redact in
   the file, and whether to rewrite history.
2. ~~**API versioning (P4)** is breaking ŌĆö confirm strategy
   (`/shepard/api/v1` prefix, dual-serve, deprecation window) before
   dispatching.~~ ŌĆö **resolved**: shipped non-breaking. Upstream
   `/shepard/api/...` stays byte-frozen via explicit class-level
   `@Path("/shepard/api/...")` prefix; new fork-additive endpoints land
   under `/v2/` (per `CLAUDE.md` API-version policy). User-facing URLs
   unchanged.
3. **Templates system (L3)** is large and design-heavy ŌĆö needs a written
   design before implementation.
4. **Neo4J ID migration (L2)** is large and touches a lot of code ŌĆö needs
   a written design before implementation.
5. **Admin role mechanism (A0)** ŌĆö A3b discovered there is no admin auth
   in shepard today. JWT roles are always `new String[0]`, so
   `@RolesAllowed("admin")` denies everyone. Three paths offered:
   (a) full admin-role mechanism populating roles from OIDC claims
   (~50 lines + config), (b) dev-profile-only exposure of admin
   endpoints, (c) scope-shift admin endpoints to `/temp/admin/*` with
   the same auth as the existing `/temp/migrations/*` carve-out and
   harden later. Affects A3b, P3c.
6. **R-series items (R1ŌĆōR9)** from the second-pass input analysis are
   mostly blocked on design / framework / asset decisions ŌĆö see
   "Newly surfaced" table.

## Round log

### Round 1 ŌĆö 2026-05-05

Dispatched two small, well-isolated agents in parallel worktrees.
Their output lands as separate commits on this branch.

| ID | Agent description | Status | Commit | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| A1 | Bounded-timeout DB connection wait with exponential backoff | done | `a74d278` | Replaces infinite loops in `MigrationsRunner.waitForConnection` and `NeoConnector`. Adds `ConnectionWaitTimeoutException`, 5-test `MigrationsRunnerTest` (deterministic via injected clock+sleeper). Spawned follow-ups A1d, A1e. |
| A4 | Caffeine-backed permission cache with TTL/LRU | done | `53996a3` | Cache was already Caffeine via `quarkus-cache`; landed per-cache TTL/max-size config + 5-test behavioural contract. Spawned follow-ups A4c (warming), A4d (metrics). |

**Round 1 outcome:** both items landed cleanly on the dispatcher branch.
A1 + A4 land 357 lines added across 7 files (5 prod, 2 test) with 9 new
unit tests, all passing. Two stale assumptions in `input_raw.md` were
corrected on the way (A1: the analysis flagged Mongo/Timescale/PostGIS
infinite waits, but only Neo4j had them in this codebase; A4: the
permission cache was already Caffeine-backed, not a basic Map).

### Round 2 ŌĆö 2026-05-05

Dispatched 5 agents in parallel worktrees. P3, A1b, and A1e all sit in
the migrations / startup / health area, so cherry-pick conflicts are
possible ŌĆö explicit non-overlap clauses included in each prompt:

- A1e owns `MigrationsRunner.java` (just the catch blocks).
- A1b owns health-check classes; explicitly told **not** to touch
  `MigrationsRunner` / `NeoConnector` / Neo4j common.
- P3 owns the InfluxDBŌåÆTimescaleDB migration tool (separate module);
  expected to be disjoint from A1b/A1e.

L5 (API keys) and A3 (feature toggles) are independent of all of the above.

**Round 2 outcome:** all 5 items landed on the dispatcher branch.
~3,200 lines added across ~60 files, **102 new unit tests** all passing
on the merged branch (8 `MigrationsRunner` + 21 health-check + 9 API-key
+ 2 versioning toggle + 17 migration progress + 5 from earlier round +
existing regressions). Two cherry-pick conflicts resolved manually:
- `MigrationsRunnerTest.java` (A1 vs A1e ŌĆö combined test sets).
- `application.properties` (A1 vs A3 ŌĆö kept both new keys).
Three stale spots in `input_raw.md` were corrected during dispatch:
- A1: only Neo4j had infinite waits, not Mongo/Timescale/PostGIS.
- A4: cache was already Caffeine, not a basic Map.
- P3: orchestrator image source lives outside this repo; only the
  COPY path was instrumentable here.

### Round 4 ŌĆö 2026-05-05 (analysis layer)

While Round 3 implementation agents ran, four parallel **analysis-only**
agents produced strategic / design docs requested by the maintainer:

| Doc | Purpose | Status | Commit |
|---|---|---|---|
| `aidocs/platform/19-architecture-feedback.md` | Critical review of post-Round-3 architecture | done | `879ffc0` |
| `aidocs/platform/20-epic-roadmap.md` | 14-epic catalogue with Mermaid dependency graph + 2-track 6-month plan | done | `fc4ae3b` |
| `aidocs/archive/21-user-interest-gauge.md` | Demand signals for HDF5/HSDS, tabular, KG interfaces + survey plan | done | `362712e` |
| `aidocs/ops/22-admin-cli-draft.md` | Candidate functions for a future `shepard-admin` CLI | done | `452eded` |

**Key findings from these docs that should drive Round 4 priorities:**

- **`aidocs/19` flags two security fragilities at the top:**
  - **C3 fallback** at `PermissionsService.java:262+` ŌĆö when the
    permissions node is missing, the fallback grants Reader+Writer+Manager.
    This is a full-access backdoor catalogued in
    `aidocs/archive/07-security-issues.md` C3 ŌĆö **not new, but not yet fixed**.
  - **C5 Cypher injection** at `Neo4jQueryBuilder.java:198-244` ŌĆö
    string-concatenated query construction; cross-cuts every search
    endpoint and gates `aidocs/semantics/13-search-improvements.md`.
  - Plus **A0** (admin role) ŌĆö already in our backlog.
- **`aidocs/20` recommends two parallel tracks:**
  - **Foundations track:** E1 (foundations: A0 + observability + P4 + L6 + S1) ŌåÆ E5 (streaming + ID alignment) ŌåÆ E11 (permissions + admin CLI) ŌåÆ E2 (unified search v2).
  - **User-value track:** E12 (UX & ecosystem) ŌåÆ E6 (annotation generalisation) ŌåÆ E9 (spatial graduate/deprecate) ŌåÆ E4 (triplestore + SPARQL).
  - Three "could start tomorrow" epics: **E1, E5, E12**.
  - Three "blocked on user decision" epics: **E14** (Neo4j ID migration owner), **E9** (spatial graduate vs deprecate), **E4** (default ontology + reasoning profile + n10s deployment).
- **`aidocs/21` ranks the three candidate development directions:**
  - **KG interfaces:** strongest evidence (4 open GitLab issues, partial `SparqlConnector` already, two independent user groups). Ready to act once #274 unblocks.
  - **HDF5/HSDS:** low-medium; one named asker, no GitLab issue, TimescaleDB satisfies the temporal subset. **Maintainer-confirmed hard constraint (2026-05-05):** any HDF5 surface must be compatible with the existing Python ecosystem (`h5py` / `PyTables` / `pandas.read_hdf`) ŌĆö `h5pyd` over HSDS is the canonical access path; "download original file" is the fallback. Recorded in epic E7 (`aidocs/platform/20-epic-roadmap.md:309-329`) and ┬¦3.6 of `aidocs/archive/21-user-interest-gauge.md`.
  - **Tabular/relational:** thin; the ask hides two distinct products (interface vs storage). Defer until separated.

| TM1 | Time Reference Model ŌĆö `timeReference: enum WALL_CLOCK \| EXPERIMENT_RELATIVE` + `wallClockOffset: long` (nanoseconds epoch of t=0 in stored data) on `TimeseriesReference`. Both fields mutable via `PATCH /v2/timeseries-references/{appId}` ŌĆö offset can be corrected any time a better anchor is discovered (ffprobe, SA sync signal, manual). Translation: `wall_clock_ns(sample) = wallClockOffset + sample_t_ns`. Optional `wallClockOffsetSource: String` tag ("manual" / "ffprobe" / "SA_sync" / "NTP_marker"). V-series Cypher migration backfills `timeReference="WALL_CLOCK"` on all existing rows. | PERF2b | Recommender ŌĆö `scripts/perf/recommend.py` reads `last-run.json` + Prometheus instant queries ŌåÆ 3-5 ranked suggestions | user request 2026-05-12, `aidocs/59 ┬¦4` | M | **Ō£ō shipped** | `scripts/perf/recommend.py`. stdlib-only Python 3.9+. Six rules: `search_threshold_breach` (k6 p95 > 3000ms ŌåÆ Neo4j page-cache), `collections_threshold_breach` (k6 p95 > 800ms ŌåÆ perms-cache), `jvm_heap_too_small` (heap > 85% ŌåÆ -Xmx), `gc_pauses_high` (GC max > 200ms ŌåÆ G1GC), `permissions_cache_cold` (hit rate < 60% ŌåÆ cache size + TTL), `mongo_latency_high` (avg cmd > 50ms ŌåÆ pool size). Prometheus queries for JVM heap, GC pause, perms-cache hit ratio, Mongo latency; falls back gracefully when Prometheus is unreachable. `--json` for machine-readable output; `--output FILE`; `--dry-run` uses canned data. Exit 0 = healthy, exit 1 = suggestions found (CI-friendly), exit 2 = error. |

The cipher format includes a `gcm1:` prefix marker so a future cipher upgrade can recognise the legacy shape. **Versioned PIDs (KIP1h respect)**: `DataciteMinter` reads `MintRequest.versionNumber()` directly (KIP1h made it a first-class field), encodes as `version: "v<n>"` in the DataCite request body, and adds `relatedIdentifiers: [{ relationType: IsNewVersionOf, ... }]` for n > 1 ŌĆö plus a back-fill `PUT /dois/<previous>` that stamps the inverse `HasVersion` so the chain renders both ways in DataCite Commons. Previous-PID lookup is delegated to a `PreviousPublicationResolver` interface that defaults to a no-op (test-friendly; production wires it to the in-core `PublicationDAO` via the manifest hook). **Network hardening**: 10s connect + 30s request timeout on the JDK `HttpClient`; one retry on 5xx / network exception with 1s backoff; `MinterException` on second failure (caught by core `PublishService` ŌåÆ 500 `publish.minter.failed`). 4xx is final (no retry). **Resource-type mapping**: shepard's `digitalObjectType` (Dataset / Collection / Software / Text / Image) maps onto DataCite's `resourceTypeGeneral` vocabulary with `Dataset` as the safe default. **Event mapping**: DataCite `event` field set from `defaultState` ŌĆö `draft`/`registered`/`findable` ŌåÆ `draft`/`register`/`publish`. New tests: 126 cases across 9 classes (`DataciteMinterTest` 30, `DataciteMinterConfigServiceTest` 24, `DataciteAdminRestTest` 17, `DataciteCommandsTest` 22, `CredentialCipherTest` 12, `DataciteIoTest` 7, `MintersAdminCliCommandProviderTest` 5, `DataciteMinterConfigTest` 5, `DataciteMinterPluginManifestTest` 4). Migration: `V33__Add_appId_constraint_DataciteMinterConfig.cypher` (V31 + V32 are taken by KIP1h backfill + PM1e PluginRuntimeOverride). New deploy-time keys (install defaults that seed the singleton on first start): `shepard.minters.datacite.{enabled,api-base-url,handle-prefix,repository-id,publisher,landing-page-base,default-state}`. Password is NOT a deploy-time key (security posture; gitleaks would flag it). Default `api-base-url=https://api.test.datacite.org` (Fabrica test environment). Operator runbook: `docs/reference/minter-datacite.md`. ### MCPGW ŌĆö 2026-05-22 (MCP gateway as sync SSOT)

User directive 2026-05-22: *"move syncservice into mcpgateway ŌĆ” config ui? complete sync ŌĆö mcpgateway explicit source of truth. additional services on lobe require explicit confirmation (one time on gui)"*.

Consolidates sync into the MCP gateway plugin (`shepard-plugin-mcp`) and gives operators an explicit confirmation gate when client-side LLM hosts (LobeChat, Claude Desktop, etc.) request to add new shepard-backed services.

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|

Remove the separate SyncService deployment surface. | M | queued | Cross-cutting refactor ŌĆö SyncService likely currently lives outside the plugin module. Need to enumerate which collections/containers it sync-watches today + map to the MCP gateway's resource model. Depends on shepard-plugin-mcp being the canonical surface (MCP1d already shipped per task #30). |
| MCPGW-SYNC2 | Config UI for sync: list of services + their sync state + add/remove buttons. | MCPGW-SYNC3 | "Additional services on lobe require explicit confirmation" ŌĆö when LobeChat / Claude Desktop / any client requests a new service binding via the MCP `tools/discover` flow, the gateway holds the request in a `pending-approval` state. An operator clicks **Confirm once** on the GUI (per-client, one-time) and the service is then exposed thereafter. | M | queued | Anti-abuse posture: a compromised LobeChat instance cannot silently expand the surface area it can reach. ### ID-MIG ŌĆö 2026-05-23 (appId ŌåÆ shepardId transition migration ŌĆö operator story)

User directive 2026-05-23: *"backlog appId to shepardId transition migration"*. Pre-existing context (consulted per `feedback_backlog_consult_context.md`):

- **Design done:** `aidocs/platform/25-neo4j-id-migration-design.md` (L2 chain), `aidocs/platform/87-timeseries-appid-migration.md` (TS variant), `aidocs/platform/91-appid-uri-scheme.md` (URI scheme).
- **Code-rename rule:** `feedback_appid_to_shepardid.md` in agent memory ŌĆö single coordinated rename pass, NOT ad-hoc.
- **Shipped:** L2a (`fec7979`) additive `appId` property; L2b (`796bc11`) backfill; L2c (`f3ca003`) Cypher rewrites. L2d (v2 surface exposes appId) **gated on H4** (now shipped ŌĆö L2d ready to land).
- **Sibling backlog rows:** task #58 (TS 5-tupleŌåÆshepardId), task #123 (Java internal rename, deferred until SHACL substrate lands), task #125 (rename PRs 3-10 sweep).

The rows below cover what's **missing** ŌĆö the operator-facing transition story (deprecation window, dual-emit, comms, migration tooling).

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| ID-MIG1 | **Dual-emit window** ŌĆö every `/v2/` response that today emits `appId` also emits `shepardId` (same UUIDv7 value, both keys present). Both are accepted on inbound. Compat surface `/shepard/api/...` stays appId-only (byte-frozen per CLAUDE.md). Adds a `Deprecation: true` + `Sunset: <date>` header on responses still using `appId`. | M | queued | Builds on L2d. Cite `aidocs/91 ┬¦URI-scheme` for the canonical `shepard:<instance>:<kind>:<id>` resolution. Dual-emit is the bridge before ID-MIG2. |
| ID-MIG2 | **Code-side rename (the field, not the value)** ŌĆö Java field/method/JSON-name pass `appId` ŌåÆ `shepardId` across backend + frontend + MCP + generated clients. SAME UUIDv7 value; just the property name moves. Bundle into ONE coordinated PR train per `feedback_appid_to_shepardid.md`. Cite #123 + #125 as the pre-existing rows. | XL | queued | Single coordinated pass. Pre-conditions: ID-MIG1 dual-emit shipped + L2d shipped + SHACL substrate split decision made (`feedback_shacl_single_source_of_truth.md`). Do NOT start this before SHACL stabilises or the rename happens on top of a moving target. |
| ID-MIG3 | **`shepard-admin migrate-appid` CLI verb** ŌĆö operator-side data export / re-key tool. | ID-MIG4 | **Operator comms package** ŌĆö `aidocs/34` row for the dual-emit + the rename PR + a deprecation roadmap; `docs/admin.md` "what changed" section; `docs/reference/api.md` field-by-field mapping (`appId` ŌåÆ `shepardId`); banner on the GitHub Pages site for the duration of the window; release-note ladder. | S | queued | Comms-only. Lands with ID-MIG1 (dual-emit) for awareness, fires again with ID-MIG2 (cutover). |
| ID-MIG5 | **L2e cutover** ŌĆö drop the upstream `/v1/` long-id paths after the deprecation window. Gated on ID-MIG2 + ID-MIG3 shipped + operator-window expiry. Per CLAUDE.md `/shepard/api/...` stays byte-frozen ŌĆö only the new `/v2/...` surface drops legacy `appId` field. |

### DB-OPT ŌĆö 2026-05-23 (database optimisation against real-world data ŌĆö POST-IMPORT)

User directive 2026-05-23: *"after import we should do the database optimisation case we have real word data"*. The MFFD ingest is about to populate the multi-substrate stack with the first **real-world-scale** dataset (Ōēł8k DataObjects + their reference graph + tapelaying TS + bridgewelding TS). That's the perfect baseline for benchmark-driven optimisation. Sequencing: import lands ŌåÆ snapshot the post-import state ŌåÆ run the DB-OPT pass against real data ŌåÆ ship the wins. Builds on `### DB ŌĆö 2026-05-22` inventory + anti-pattern hunt; this section is the **action layer**.

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| DB-OPT1 | **Capture the post-import baseline** ŌĆö once MFFD ingest completes, snapshot every store: Neo4j node + relationship counts per label, Postgres table sizes + index hit-rates, TimescaleDB chunk count + compression ratio, MongoDB collection sizes, PostGIS geometry counts, Garage bucket size. Output: `aidocs/agent-findings/db-baseline-post-mffd.md`. This is the reference point every optimisation is measured against. | S | queued | Blocks DB-OPT2..5. Should run automatically as the final step of the import script's `--verify-imported` flag in a future v15.3. |
| DB-OPT2 | **Hot-path query analysis** ŌĆö `EXPLAIN ANALYZE` every Postgres query the backend issues on `/v2/collections/{appId}`, `/v2/timeseries-containers/{appId}/timeseries`, `/v2/collections/{appId}/data-objects` against the real MFFD data. Same for Neo4j `PROFILE` of the Cypher analogs. Output: ranked list of queries by latency + plan + suggested index. Wins land as a `V##__add_index_hot_path.{sql,cypher}` migration. | M | queued | Real-world data is the only honest signal here; synthetic LUMEN data has wrong cardinality. |
| DB-OPT3 | **Timeseries-specific tuning** ŌĆö TimescaleDB chunk interval vs MFFD's actual ingest cadence (likely 1ms TCP thermal trail ŌåÆ micro-batches), compression policy on chunks older than N days, continuous-aggregate candidates for the dashboard endpoints. | M | queued | Cite `aidocs/platform/87-timeseries-appid-migration.md` for the substrate model. |
| DB-OPT4 | **Anti-pattern remediation pass** ŌĆö the DB-AP1 / DB-AP2 hunt rows in the `### DB ŌĆö` section produced findings; this row ships the fixes on the real data. Per-substrate: rebuild missing indices, drop dead ones, fix dual-source-of-truth fields, add TTLs where data is ephemeral. | L | queued | Depends on DB-AP1+AP2 completing. Real data may surface different priorities than the synthetic baseline did. |
| DB-OPT5 | **Frontend payload diet** ŌĆö once query latency is honest, the next round of wins is on response-shape. Use the actual `/v2/collections/{appId}/data-objects` payload size on MFFD-Dropbox (Ōēł8k DOs ├Ś ~2 KB each = 16 MB) and figure out which fields the frontend actually reads. Slim the response by `?fields=` or default-trim heavy nested objects. | M | queued | Pairs with the existing pagination work (task #51 + #112). |
| DB-OPT6 | **Operator runbook** ŌĆö `docs/ops/db-optimisation-runbook.md`: how an admin of a downstream Shepard fork instance runs the same optimisation pass against their own data. Templated `EXPLAIN ANALYZE` queries + interpretation cheat-sheet. | S | queued | Mirrors `docs/ops/garage-activation-runbook.md` shape. |

### DB ŌĆö 2026-05-22 (database inventory + best-practices + anti-pattern hunt)

User directive 2026-05-22: *"database inverntiry best pracices review, antipattern avaidance on backlog"*. Survey the full multi-substrate landscape (Neo4j + Postgres + TimescaleDB + MongoDB + PostGIS + Garage S3) and codify what's good, what's drifting, and what's actively anti-pattern. Per `feedback_db_review_all_stores.md` ŌĆö never single out one substrate.

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| DB-INV1 | **Inventory pass** ŌĆö every Cypher migration (`V##__*.cypher`), every Flyway SQL migration (`db/migration/V*.sql`), every Mongo collection seed, every PostGIS geometry table, every Garage bucket. Output: `aidocs/data/<NN>-db-inventory.md` listing schema name + owner module + indices + active write-paths. | M | queued | Snapshot in time; refresh annually. Cross-references CLAUDE.md "always ship migrations idempotent + fail-fast". |
| DB-BP1 | **Best-practices catalogue** ŌĆö what the fork does right per store. Examples: parametrised Cypher (post-C5/C5b shipped), JPA `@Entity` + Panache repository pattern (importer plugin), PostGIS index-on-create, Mongo collection naming convention. Each entry cites a representative commit. Output: `aidocs/data/<NN>-db-best-practices.md`. | M | queued | Living catalogue. Authors of new code copy from here. |
| DB-AP1 | **Anti-pattern hunt** ŌĆö find every site that violates a known good practice. Candidates: string-concat'd Cypher (C5/C5b killed them but regressions grow back), N+1 query patterns (Neo4j AND Postgres), missing indices on hot-path foreign keys, GridFS used for files when Garage S3 is active, missing `ON DELETE CASCADE` on Postgres FKs where the parent is mutable, missing constraints on `:HasAppId` Neo4j labels, Mongo collections without TTL where the data is ephemeral. Output: `aidocs/agent-findings/db-antipatterns.md` listing every flagged site with severity (CRITICAL/MAJOR/MINOR) and remediation. | L | queued | Dispatched as multi-agent fan-out (one agent per substrate). Per `feedback_db_review_all_stores.md` MUST cover all six substrates. |
| DB-AP2 | **Cross-cutting findings** ŌĆö patterns that span substrates. E.g. dual-source-of-truth (same field written to Neo4j AND Postgres), substrate-mismatch (timeseries lives in Timescale but the Neo4j `:Timeseries` label still carries denormalised metadata that can drift), schema-evolution gaps (migration added the field but the IO class doesn't surface it). Highest-value findings per SSOT discipline (`feedback_shacl_single_source_of_truth.md`). | M | queued | DB-AP1 enables DB-AP2 ŌĆö run AP1 first per substrate, then AP2 reads the union. |
| DB-DOC1 | Roll the catalogues into operator-facing docs: `docs/reference/database-overview.md` (one-screen "what data lives where") + `docs/help/troubleshooting-databases.md` (operator-readable common issues + fixes). | S | queued | Last step. Surfaces the inventory to the Pages site. |

### P1 ŌĆö 2026-05-16 (parallel DB connectivity)

| ID | Slice | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| P1 | Parallel startup DB warm + parallel recovery | done | New `DbConnectivityWarmer` (`@ApplicationScoped`, `@Observes StartupEvent`) fires one `Thread.ofVirtual()` per required `DbPinger` in parallel ŌĆö total startup wait is now `max(latencies)` not `sum(latencies)`. Bounded by `shepard.migrations.connection-wait-timeout` (reused from `MigrationsRunner`; no new config key). `DbRecoveryScheduler.attemptRecovery()` now collects stale pingers then probes each in its own virtual thread (`CompletableFuture.allOf` blocks the tick). Both use `RequestContextController.activate/deactivate` per thread so JPA `EntityManager` injections in `TimescalePinger` / `PostGisPinger` work correctly off the caller thread. Per-DB `DbHealthState` independently tracks each outcome. 7 new unit tests in `DbConnectivityWarmerTest` (including timing proof: 3 ├Ś 300 ms pingers finish in < 950 ms wall-clock); 2 new tests added to `DbRecoverySchedulerTest`. |

### VIS ŌĆö 2026-05-22 (visualization plugin family)

Survey: `aidocs/agent-findings/vis-plugin-survey.md`. Broadens the Trace3D seed
(`aidocs/agent-findings/trace3d-spike.md`, task #142) into a coherent plugin
family covering 3D paths/traces, vector fields/CFD, voxel/volumetric (REM/EM/╬╝CT),
and surface meshes. **Extended 2026-05-22** with categories 5 (CAD data) and
6 (FEM result files) per
`aidocs/agent-findings/vis-plugin-survey-addendum-cad-fem.md` ŌĆö
7 categories total, 5 plugins + 2 sidecars. All rows queued; pick-up order:
VIS-S1 ŌåÆ VIS-T1 ŌåÆ VIS-V1 ŌåÆ VIS-X1 ŌåÆ **VIS-C1 ŌåÆ VIS-F1** ŌåÆ VIS-S2 ŌåÆ VIS-S3
(stretch).

**Critical context for VIS-T1:** `@tresjs/nuxt` repo was archived Feb 1, 2026.
`@tresjs/core` itself (v5.8.1, May 2026) is still actively maintained. Use core
directly via an in-plugin `useTres()` composable; do NOT depend on the archived
Nuxt module. This is a correction to `aidocs/agent-findings/trace3d-spike.md`
which assumed `@tresjs/nuxt` was available ŌĆö see survey ┬¦1.2 for the rationale.

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |

| VIS-S1 | Shared cross-cutting platform piece: `POST /v2/shapes/render` `ViewRecipeRenderer` SPI dispatcher (in-tree, plugin authors register a `Resolver` keyed by templateName) + Garage signed-URL minter helper (`SignedUrlIssuer`) + presigned-URL access-control filter | M | queued | In-tree, not a plugin. **Predecessor for all VIS-* plugins.** Already partially scoped in `aidocs/agent-findings/trace3d-spike.md ┬¦3` and `aidocs/agent-findings/persona-review-api-scrutinizer.md`. |
| VIS-T1 | `shepard-plugin-vis-trace3d` module skeleton + `Trace3DViewShape` + `MeshViewShape` SHACL allow-list extension + `TraceFrameResolver` (TS channels ŌåÆ aligned frames per `aidocs/agent-findings/trace3d-spike.md ┬¦3` envelope) + `Trace3DView.vue` (`@tresjs/core` 5.8 via in-plugin `useTres()` composable, Line2 fat-line shader, vertex colours via inferno/viridis/etc. colour maps) + `MeshView.vue` (Three.js `GLTFLoader` + `STLLoader`) + `TimeScrubber.vue` + plugin docs trio (`reference.md`/`quickstart.md`/`install.md`) | L (~2 sprints) | queued | Use `@tresjs/core` directly; **NOT** the archived `@tresjs/nuxt` module (archived Feb 2026). | VIS-V1 | `shepard-plugin-vis-vector` module skeleton + `VectorFieldViewShape` SHACL allow-list extension + `VectorFieldResolver` (structured payload ŌåÆ `.vti`/`.vtu` VTK XML on Garage with signed URL) + `VtkScene.vue` (generic Vue Ōåö VTK.js mount helper, shared with vis-volume; modelled on `Kitware/vue-vtk-js`) + `VectorFieldView.vue` (vtkStreamTracer / vtkGlyph3DMapper / vtkLineIntegralConvolution2D, switched by `renderMode` slot: `streamlines` \| `lic` \| `arrows` \| `particle-trace`) + plugin docs trio | M | queued | VTK.js v35 (BSD-3-Clause, Kitware, March 2026). | VIS-X1 | `shepard-plugin-vis-volume` module skeleton + `VolumeViewShape` SHACL allow-list extension + `VolumeResolver` (file payload ŌåÆ OME-Zarr pyramid URL via `vtkjs-inline` render target OR Neuroglancer state URL via `neuroglancer-iframe` render target, switched by `renderTarget` slot) + `VolumeView.vue` (branches `<VtkScene>` vs `<NeuroglancerIframe>`) + `TransferFunctionEditor.vue` (piecewise-linear opacity + RGB editor, Vuetify dialog) + `volume-pyramidiser` sidecar (Python FastAPI + `ome-zarr-py` + `tifffile` + `pydicom`; produces multi-resolution OME-Zarr pyramid on Garage on file upload; declared in manifest per PM1f / `feedback_plugins_declare_sidecars.md`) + plugin docs trio | L (~3 sprints) | queued | Two render targets, one plugin (VTK.js inline for Ōēż 1 GB stacks; Neuroglancer iframe for OME-Zarr / N5 / TB-scale EM). Largest competitive moat in the family ŌĆö almost no competing RDM platform ships in-the-box volume viewing. |
| VIS-C1 | `shepard-plugin-vis-cad` module skeleton + `CadViewShape` SHACL allow-list extension + `CadResolver` (File payload ŌåÆ signed Garage URL for `occt-inline` track, or triggers optional `step-to-gltf-converter` sidecar for `gltf-cached` track, or constructs iframe URL for `online3dviewer-iframe` fallback) + `CadView.vue` (`occt-import-js` WASM browser-side STEP/IGES/BREP read + tessellation ŌåÆ Three.js `BufferGeometry` inside shared `<TresCanvas>` from `vis-trace3d`) + `AssemblyTree.vue` (Vuetify treeview from occt-import-js hierarchy result; click-to-isolate) + `SectionPlaneControls.vue` (three-slider Vuetify dialog applying Three.js `Clipping Plane`) + `CadIframe.vue` (Online3DViewer iframe wrapper for exotic formats ŌĆö `.CATPart`, `.prt`) + plugin docs trio (`reference`/`quickstart`/`install`) | L (~2 sprints) | queued | `occt-import-js` is LGPL-2.1 ŌĆö **not** in the CLAUDE.md GPL/AGPL/SSPL ban list; dynamic-linking clause satisfied as WASM blob loaded at runtime; documented in `plugins/vis-cad/docs/install.md`. **xeokit-sdk rejected** (AGPLv3 ŌĆö blocked by licence gate). **Forge Viewer rejected** (commercial). `Online3DViewer` (MIT, kovacsv) ŌĆö widest format coverage on the web (3dm, 3ds, brep, dae, fbx, fcstd, gltf, ifc, iges, step, stl, obj, off, ply, wrl) ŌĆö ships as static SPA at `cdn.shepard/online3dviewer/v1/` for the iframe fallback track. Optional `step-to-gltf-converter` Python sidecar (`pythonocc-core` LGPL + FastAPI; declared per PM1f, opt-in only) for assemblies > ~50 MB or > ~5k parts where in-browser WASM tessellation grinds. Acceptance: MFFD upper-fuselage CATIA STEP (~80 MB, ~2k parts) renders in < 15 s cold / < 3 s warm; section-plane drag at > 24 FPS; as-designed (STEP) vs as-built (STL laser-scanner) overlay diff in one scene. ### M4I ŌĆö 2026-05-23 (metadata4ing deepening)

User directive 2026-05-23: *"how to deepen metadata4ing (m4i) integration"*.
Design lands at `aidocs/semantics/94-metadata4ing-integration-design.md`.
**Critical finding** surfaced during research: the current
`ProvJsonLdRenderer` emits **non-canonical predicates**
(`m4i:hasMethod` / `m4i:hasInput` / `m4i:hasOutput`) that do
not exist in canonical m4i 1.4.0 ŌĆö see M4I-b. Latest m4i
version is **1.4.0 (2025-12-08)**; the shipped bundle pins it
already, no version bump needed.

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| M4I-a | Promote `metadata4ing.ttl` stub ŌåÆ fetch canonical TTL on first seed via existing `canonicalUrl` + `fetchOnSeed` flag (NASA Thesaurus N1e pattern). Stub stays in JAR as offline fallback. Acceptance: Ōēź 100 m4i `:Resource` rows in n10s after fresh start. | S (1 d) | queued | `aidocs/semantics/94 ┬¦4.1`. Builds on `aidocs/44 ┬¦7a` N1e precedent + `aidocs/semantics/65 ┬¦2.3` canonical-URL pattern. No backend Java churn beyond a flag flip on the manifest entry. |
| M4I-b | **CRITICAL bug-shaped fix.** Rewrite m4i branch of `ProvJsonLdRenderer.render(...)` to emit canonical predicates: `m4i:hasMethod` ŌåÆ **`m4i:realizesMethod`**; `m4i:hasInput` ŌåÆ **`obo:RO_0002233`** (OBO Relations Ontology, already preseeded via ONT1a); `m4i:hasOutput` ŌåÆ **`obo:RO_0002234`**. Extend `@context` with `"obo"` prefix when profile=m4i. Add `m4i:investigates` from activity to investigated entity on read actions. | S (1 d) | queued | `aidocs/semantics/94 ┬¦4.2`. Verified against canonical OWL at `https://nfdi4ing.pages.rwth-aachen.de/metadata4ing/metadata4ing/` on 2026-05-23. Add SHACL self-test asserting canonical predicates. AWARE in `aidocs/34` flagged BREAKING for any m4i consumer that depended on the old non-canonical names (low real-world risk; no known consumer; discipline is the point). |
| M4I-c | `m4i:DataObjectShape` SHACL contract + `M4iDataObjectRenderer` + content-neg `Accept: application/ld+json; profile=metadata4ing` on `GET /v2/data-objects/{appId}` (mirrors PROV1h on `/v2/provenance/*`). Mandatory triples: `m4i:InvestigatedObject` type, `dcterms:identifier`, `dcterms:title`, `schema:dateCreated`. Optional: `m4i:hasIdentifier` (KIP1a PID), `obo:RO_0002233/4` (predecessor / successor), `prov:wasGeneratedBy` (most-recent Activity), `m4i:realizesMethod` (when actionKind known), `schema:keywords` (annotations). Refactor UH1b renderer to consume same shape. | M (3ŌĆō4 d) | queued | `aidocs/semantics/94 ┬¦4.3`. Depends on M4I-a + M4I-b. Conceptually slots under `aidocs/semantics/95` SHACL substrate; ships before full substrate by reading the shape file at startup the same way ontology bundles do. Acceptance: pyShacl validation passes on every DataObject in MFFD + LUMEN seed Collections. |
| M4I-d | Promote `:Activity.actionKind` / instruments / annotations to first-class m4i individuals. Three sub-slices: **(d-1)** mint stable `shepard:method/<kind>` IRIs typed `m4i:Method` on first use; **(d-2)** mint `shepard:tool/<typename>` IRIs typed `m4i:Tool`, link via `m4i:hasEmployedTool`; **(d-3)** annotation keys matching SHACL `m4i:hasNumericalVariable` slot render as typed `m4i:NumericalVariable` blank nodes with QUDT unit refs. | M (3 d) | queued | `aidocs/semantics/94 ┬¦4.4`. Depends on M4I-c (shape contract for what counts as a numeric variable). Acceptance: SPARQL `?step m4i:realizesMethod ?m. ?m a m4i:Method.` returns Ōēź 1 row over MFFD seed. Read-time computation (lazy promotion) ŌĆö no write-throughput hit. |
| M4I-e | Operator runbook `docs/reference/nfdi4ing-federation.md` + companion task page `docs/help/register-with-nfdi4ing.md`. Walk through: m4i bundle enable verification ŌåÆ Terminology Service self-registration ŌåÆ Unhide harvester pointing ŌåÆ (forward-looking) NFDI4Ing Archetype Doris registration for HPMC use cases. Pure docs, no code. | S (1 d) | queued | `aidocs/semantics/94 ┬¦4.5`. Pairs with `aidocs/integrations/67 ┬¦7`. Acceptance: real ZLP Augsburg / Lampoldshausen operator can follow it end-to-end in Ōēż 30 min. |
| M4I-f | Add `metadata4ing-hpmc` bundle to preseed manifest ŌĆö m4i HPMC sub-ontology for high-performance measurement + computing workflows. SHA-256-pinned TTL stub + canonical URL + `required=false`, default-on. Stub covers headline classes (`m4i:HpmcWorkflow` etc.); N1c admin refresh pulls full canonical OWL. | S (1 d) | queued | `aidocs/semantics/94 ┬¦4.6`. Source: <https://nfdi4ing.de/5-23-2/>. Targeted (HPMC-using operators only ŌĆö LUMEN hot-fire DAQ, MFFD AFP telemetry). Parallel to M4I-a. Document transitive dependencies (potentially NFDI-MatWerk / MaRDI terms) in the bundle's manifest entry. |

Recommended landing order (per `aidocs/semantics/94 ┬¦9`):
**M4I-a ŌåÆ M4I-b ŌåÆ M4I-c ŌåÆ M4I-e ŌåÆ M4I-d ŌåÆ M4I-f**. Total ~10ŌĆō11 days.
M4I-b lands first regardless of slice ordering ŌĆö correctness, not deepening.

### SWEEP ŌĆö 2026-05-23 (deferred items surfaced from repo grep)

Sweep result from a cross-cutting `grep -E 'TODO|FIXME|deferred|follow-up|out of scope|queued'` pass across `backend/`, `frontend/`, `plugins/`, `examples/`, `docs/`, `aidocs/agent-findings/`, `aidocs/{platform,integrations,ops,semantics,strategy,ux,workflows,reference}/*.md`, `.github/workflows/`, `Makefile`, and `backend/pom.xml`. 320 existing row IDs were extracted from this file and used as a dedup filter ŌĆö every row below is **not** already on the backlog. Full inventory + source citations: `aidocs/agent-findings/repo-task-sweep-2026-05-23.md`.

Rationale: per `feedback_backlog_for_later.md` ("things-for-later go on a maintained backlog, not in prose docs") and `feedback_backlog_consult_context.md` (every row cites its source). The risk being closed is the slow rot where a `TODO(IMP1)` in `ImportV2Rest.java` or a "this is a follow-up" footnote in a design doc never becomes a row, and the deferral is forgotten.

Skew: 5 CRITICAL, 49 MAJOR, 17 MINOR, 14 NICE-to-have. Highest-priority item to ship: **`MFG5`** ŌĆö enforce DataObject `status` as a closed enum at the persistence boundary. Quoting `aidocs/agent-findings/manufacturing-quality.md ┬¦11.2`: *"the single largest gap between Shepard's current design and aerospace quality record requirements"* ŌĆö one backend PR, no migration on shipped data beyond a value-set check.

| MFFD-IMPORT-PERF1 | **Real worker fan-out for `run_source_mode_workers`.** Extract the per-DO loop body (`mffd-import-v15.py` L2495..2598) into a callable `_process_one_source_do(...)` and submit one future per source DO. Bound at 4 concurrent cube3 GETs + 4 dest POSTs per `aidocs/93 ┬¦5`. Today the wrapper is a fake fan-out ŌĆö it spawns the pool, runs `lambda: True` probes, then calls `run_source_mode` SEQUENTIALLY (`mffd-import-v15.py` L2983..2999). `--workers N` does nothing for throughput. | M | **done (v15.8)** | MAJOR | `aidocs/agent-findings/mffd-import-slowness-diagnose-2026-05-23.md ┬¦5 Hypothesis #1` | Shipped 2026-05-23 in v15.8 (manifest published to FileContainer 473932). Per-DO body extracted into `_process_one_source_do(src_do, do_bar)` closure inside `run_source_mode`. Driver submits one future per source DO via `ThreadPoolExecutor(max_workers=workers)` with `as_completed`-based drain + refill keeping the pool saturated. `tqdm.update(1)` happens only in the driver thread. `ImportState` gains `_lock: RLock` covering all read+write ops. `existing_names` hoisted to per-step snapshot (no N parallel calls for the same dest list). `run_source_mode_workers` simplified to a thin forwarder; tests in `tests/test_worker_pool.py` updated. |
| MFFD-IMPORT-PERF2 | **Lazy enrichment in `iter_data_objects`.** Yield a stub `SourceDO(do_id, name, attrs, ...)` with `file_refs=None / ts_refs=None / sd_refs=None`; fetch refs only when the per-DO `state.is_*_done` skip check would not fire. Today (`mffd-import-v15.py` L707..711) the script fires 3 cube3 GETs per source DO BEFORE the L2504/L2541/L2570 state-skip checks. On a fully-resumed run that's 25 371 wasted WAN round-trips for an 8 457-DO collection. | S | **done (v15.8)** | MAJOR | `aidocs/agent-findings/mffd-import-slowness-diagnose-2026-05-23.md ┬¦5 Hypothesis #2` | Shipped 2026-05-23 in v15.8 (manifest published to FileContainer 473932). `SourceDO.file_refs / ts_refs / structured_refs` now default to `None`; `iter_data_objects` yields stubs (no enrichment GETs). New `ShepardClient._load_file_refs / _load_ts_refs / _load_structured_refs` helpers fetch + cache on first access via `SourceDO._src_coll_id`. Per-DO loop body calls these AFTER per-ref state-skip would short-circuit. Fully-done DO on resume: 0 cube3 GETs (was 3). |

Full policy: `aidocs/strategy/85-github-project-management-policies.md`.

sync direction is one-way (aidocs/16 ŌåÆ Issue); the unified state machine
maps doc front-matter Ōåö aidocs/16 Status Ōåö GH `status:*` / `stage:*`
labels Ōåö Projects v2 columns byte-for-byte (see `aidocs/00-doc-stages.md`).

checklist. The end-state test is `scripts/trace-feature.sh <ID>` ŌĆö nine

### OBS ŌĆö 2026-05-23 (recursive self-observability)

The principle is documented in `feedback_shepard_measures_itself.md`:
Shepard's own ingest-rate metrics live INSIDE Shepard's TimeseriesContainer
substrate, not in a parallel observability stack. The MFFD-Dropbox import
session was the first concrete instance ŌĆö the chart updates by the same
TS chart UI a researcher already uses.

| ID | Slice | Size | Status | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| OBS-MFFD1 | `scripts/mffd-import-stats-collector.py` polls `/v2/collections/{appId}/data-objects` every 5 min, walks per-DO refs for file/TS/SD counters, runs `docker exec shepard-garage /garage bucket info shepard-files` for the object-store size, and POSTs 11 channels per tick to `TimeseriesContainer` 590324 linked to `DataObject` 590344 in the MFFD-Dropbox collection. Bootstrap is idempotent; the `TimeseriesReference` is lazily created after the first tick materialises channels (the v5 `Bug A` minItems:1 constraint, learned from v15.2). Ships a systemd timer pair (`infrastructure/systemd/mffd-import-stats-collector.{service,timer}`) so operators can replace the ad-hoc background process. Plottable via the existing TS chart UI ŌĆö no new frontend code. | S | done | Shipped 2026-05-23 (this commit). Files: `scripts/mffd-import-stats-collector.py`, `infrastructure/systemd/mffd-import-stats-collector.{service,timer}`, `docs/help/observing-an-import.md`, this row, `aidocs/data/00-model-inventory.md ┬¦8` row, `feedback_shepard_measures_itself.md`. Verified: first tick at 23:07:24Z wrote 11/11 channels (`DO=8, files=0, garage=160300 B`); second tick at 23:08:19Z saw `TSrefs=1, channels=11` confirming the lazy reference creation. |
| OBS-MFFD2 | Generalise the collector to ANY import job: lift the MFFD-specific name-pattern table into a per-collection config + accept any collection-appId. Land as `scripts/import-stats-collector.py` (drop the `mffd-` prefix) plus an admin UI for picking which collections to instrument. | M | queued | Promotes the recursive-observability pattern to a first-class tool. Pairs with the `OBS-MFFD3` admin dashboard. |
| OBS-MFFD3 | Dashboard view summarising all in-flight imports: list every `ImportStats-*` DataObject across all collections + a `dos_total` sparkline + a delta-since-last-tick. Plugs into the existing Collections list or lands as `/v2/admin/imports`. | M | queued | "What's actually being ingested right now?" admin view. Dep on `OBS-MFFD2`. Pairs with the `GH-INFRA3` release gate. |

### DOCS-3A ŌĆö 2026-05-23 (three-audience docs: admin + user + plugin)

The rule is documented in `feedback_three_audience_docs.md`: three sharply
distinct audiences (admin, user, plugin) with the same-PR maintenance shape,
served from BOTH the Pages site AND Shepard's in-app `/help` route. The user
+ plugin audiences already have policies in CLAUDE.md; the admin audience
needs explicit consolidation.

| MFFD-IMPORT-USER-CAPTURE | **v15.9 ŌĆö script captures source-side user identity for prov enrichment.** SHIPPED 2026-05-23 in v15.9 (read-side + header-forward halves). On startup `ShepardClient.resolve_self()` decodes JWT `sub` ŌåÆ GET `/shepard/api/users/{sub}` ŌåÆ caches `{username, firstName, lastName, email, effectiveDisplayName}` in module-level `SOURCE_USER_INFO`. Three forwarding channels: (a) per-DO attributes `source_user_username` + `source_user_displayName` + `source_user_email` + `source_user_instance` (visible/searchable in UI without dest plugin); (b) `X-Source-User-*` headers on every dest write (consumed by ProvenanceCaptureFilter PROV1a ŌĆö no per-call-site threading, set once on the requests.Session); (c) telemetry event `source_user_resolved` (gauge 0/1) into runlog. Dest-side `:User` mirror step deferred ŌĆö see PROV-USER-MIRROR-ENDPOINT (dest exposes no user-mint REST endpoint). Pattern card: `aidocs/integrations/95 ┬¦Pattern 17`. Tests: `examples/mffd-showcase/scripts/test_user_capture.py` (19 cases). Pairs with PROV-USER-ENRICH (dest-side header ŌåÆ PROV-O triple). | M | done (v15.9, 2026-05-23) | Read side Ō£ō + headers Ō£ō + telemetry Ō£ō. Mirror channel split out as PROV-USER-MIRROR-ENDPOINT. v5 `/users/{u}` validated working on cube3 (kreb_fl shape) + nuclide (UUID-sub shape). Graceful degradation tested (5 fallback paths). |
| PROV-USER-MIRROR-ENDPOINT | **Dest-side `:User` mirror endpoint for cross-instance prov chain.** Split out of MFFD-IMPORT-USER-CAPTURE on 2026-05-23 ŌĆö field probing found nuclide dest exposes neither `POST /v2/admin/users` (404) nor `POST /shepard/api/users` (405). User creation flows through OIDC/IDM, not REST. v15.9 emits a warning when it can't mint a mirror :User; downstream the full attribution chain ("Florian Krebs on cube3 ŌåÆ Florian Krebs on nuclide via prov:wasDerivedFrom") needs a dest endpoint. Design questions: should mirror users be a new entity subtype (`:MirroredUser` carrying `wasDerivedFrom` to source URL) or a flag on the existing `:User`? Should this be `/v2/admin/users/mirror` (admin-only, idempotent by username+source_instance pair) or part of a broader sync feed (OIDC federation)? Pairs with N1/A1 admin endpoints + PROV1a ProvenanceCaptureFilter. | M | queued | Source: 2026-05-23 (carved out during v15.9 implementation when the original spec's mirror channel hit a dead end). | MFFD-IMPORTER-DATASET-CAPTURE | **Capture the importer's version chain + the conversation transcripts that produced each version into a Shepard Collection.** Per user flag 2026-05-23: *"our transscripts about the importer should be part of the data set and the different versions, even better git references to individual changes / version of tscripts"*. One DO per importer version (v15.0..v15.9..) with `git_commit_sha` + `git_blob_url` attrs + Predecessor chain. One FileContainer with conversation-chunk fragments (`convo-chunk-NN-for-v15X.md`). Cross-references between version-DOs and transcript-fragments. Predecessor chain mirrors the version lineage. Privacy boundary: JWT/API-key scrub pass before publishing. Spec in `/root/.claude/projects/-opt-shepard/memory/project_importer_arc_as_dataset.md`. Cite via Unhide ŌåÆ DataCite ŌåÆ DOI; the Collection becomes the case-study dataset. | L | queued | Source: 2026-05-23. Ships AFTER cube3 import drains + v15.10 forward fixes + dest backfill mutations + highlights backfill (task #183). Dogfooding: Shepard manages its own development as a research dataset. |

| UX-REVERT-MUTATIONS | **First-class "undo" for data mutations ŌĆö user-facing revert of changes / mutation passes.** Companion to the Goldilocks-shaping principle (`project_mffd_dest_backfill_pass.md`, `project_dataset_forging.md`): if mutations are iterative ("juuuuuuuust right"), then UNDO must be first-class. Every mutation that lands via the v2 API is recorded as a typed `:Activity` (PROV-O) with input/output state references; the UI exposes a "history" panel per DataObject / Collection / Container showing N most recent mutations with one-click "revert this change" (returns to the pre-mutation state) and bulk "revert N passes" (back to S(N-k)). Plays nice with the snapshot chain S0ŌåÆS1ŌåÆ...ŌåÆSn that the back-fill pattern produces. Pairs with PV1a payload version history (already shipped ŌĆö extends from "file payload versions" to "attribute + reference + structure mutations"). Probably needs a v2 endpoint `POST /v2/{resource}/{appId}/revert?to=activityAppId` + `GET /v2/{resource}/{appId}/mutations` (list). | L | queued | Source: 2026-05-23 user flag ("for backlog, easy way to revert changes / mutations for users"). Companion to MFFD-IMPORTER-DATASET-CAPTURE + the dest backfill pattern. Critical for trusting AI-driven mutation passes ŌĆö user can experiment + back out safely. EN 9100 audit angle: the revert trail IS the audit trail. |
